NARA CHANDRABABU NAIDU                    '                        HYDERABAD
CHIEF  LIISTER
ANDHRA PRADESH :"
D.O.Lr.No.l 15 1S/Fin/CMP/98
Dated May 14, 1998
Dear Mr. Wolfensohn,
1.    When I met you in October 1996 in New Delhi, I explained to you our
Government's vision of putting Andhra Pradesh (AP) on a path of sustainable growth and
development withi a clear focus on enhancing the quality of life of the poorest segments of
the people. I briefed you on our agenda in this regard which, you will please recall,
included wide rarging reforms in public finance management, emphasis on education and
health, infrastructure building, and providing a rational, credible, and transparent
macroeconomic environment. The Government of Andbra Pradesh is doing all that is
possible to mobilize resources, reorient expenditure priorities, and enhance the levels of
efficiency and productivity. The purpose of this letter is to request support from
IBRD/IDA for this reform agenda. Please allow me to give you a brief background before
I proceed to discuss the various components of the reform program.
Public finance management
2.    Despite its rich resource base and physical and geographical advantages, the gross
state domestic product (GSDP) of AP has grown only by 4.6 percent a year since the early
1980s compared to the national average of 5.2 percent. This has widened the disparity in
the living standards between AP and the rest of the country. At the heart of this economic
under-performance has been the deteriorating public finance situation. The main
characteristics of this have been:
*  Falling public revenue caused by inadequate cost recovery, and a tax system
characterized by low buoyancy and complex procedures;
*  Rapidly growing salary bill and interest charges;
*  Inadequate budgetary provision for physical infrastructure and for operation
and maintenance (O&M);
contd...



-2 -                           Annex 13
page 2 Of 11
* Inadequate allocations of funds for humnan resource development, especially
primary education and public health; and
* A rapid increase in loosely targeted subsidies.
Reforms already initiated
3.    Our Government is deeply conscious of the need to reverse these trends, for failure
to do so will pull the state down in a vicious circle of poverty and stagnation. On the
other hand, a credible fiscal reform package and sector reform programs, effectively
implemented, will push it up in a virtuous circle of growth and development.  In
formulating our reforn package, we were guided by three concerns. First, there should be
a harmonious balance between welfare and development expenditure so that the income
earning; capacity of the poor is enhanced even as the truly indigent are provided social
security. Second, we must move decisively towards making government more responsive
and accountable. In this direction, we have instituted moves towards social audit, public
disclosuire of information and time limits for decisions by government. Third, we must
reckon with the fact that most adjustment programs, across the world, have failed because
of opposition from vested interests and misapprehensions of the vulnerable segments of
the population. Enlisting people's participation and support has, therefore, been a crucial
element of our strategy. Towards this end, the Government has facilitated the formation
of community based organizations in every sphere. Over the past three years, self-help
groups, watershed management committees, village development committees, village
education and village health committees, joint forest management associations, water
users' associations (WUA) etc. have been involved in decentralization of development
initiatives.
4.    Furthermore, we published a series of white papers in June 1996 explaining to the
people as simply as possible the true state of our economic and financial situation and the
maladies afflicting our public finances. The white papers generated  an extremely
rewarding debate at public fora and in the media on the options available to the
Governrment. The white papers were also discussed in a special session of the Legislative
Assembly. Based on the feedback so received, our Government initiated a number of
fiscal and sector policy measures to contain further deterioration of the fiscal situation.
These measures include:
Fiscal measures
* A policy statement describing the fiscal restructuring strategy for the state was
issued by the Government in February 1996 to initiate discussion and build
consensus on the reform program. The strategy places particular emphasis on
contd...



- 3 -                         Annex 13
page 3 of 11
changing the composition of public expenditure to improve its development
impact.
  Rice subsidy scheme was revisited and streamlined resulting in reduction of
subsidy as a percentage of GSDP from 1.6 percent to 0.7 percent in 1997-98.
*  We also rationalised the State excise policy to arrest smuggling and illicit
distillation (which incidentally contributed to increase of State revenue by
about 2.0% of GSDP).
* A staff review committee was established to examine the staffing issues in the
main Government departments. Strong measures, including a strict control on
hiring, were introduced to contain expansion of employment in the state
government. As a result of these measures, the employment declined and the
salary bill as a percentage of GSDP has come down. The composition of
employment has also changed in favor of the social sectors.
*  A broad public enterprise reform program has been initiated in the past three
years covering the state's 39 enterprises and over 40 cooperatives. A working
group was established lo recommend a reform program for each company. The
working group has already reviewed most of the small and medium size
enterprises. Its recommendations, which include privatization of several units,
closure of unviable ones, and merger and restructuring of the others, are at
various stages of approval and implementation. We have also introduced
voluntary retirement scheme (VRS) in some Public Sector Undertakings.
* Other revenue enhancing measures were taken in July 1996 including
introduction of a 1 percent turnover tax, a luxury tax on tobacco, and an 8
percent enitry tax on motor vehicles.
Power sector policies
*  We increased power tariffs considerably across all sectors.
*  A policy statement on the power sector was issued by the Government in
March 1997 to generate discussion and build support for the reform program.
The program has been widely discussed in the state with all concerned parties
including trade unions.
* Work on the preparation of a financial restructuring program for Andhra
Pradesh State Electricity Board (APSEB) has been initiated. This work is
expected to be completed in the summer of 1998.
contd...



- 4 -                           Annex 13
page 4 of 11
* A Power Sector Reform Bill was approved by the State Assembly in April
1998, which will trigger a series of reforms including establishment of an
independent regulatory authority for the power sector.
Irrigation sector policies
t Water charges for irrigation were upscaled in August 1996. The new rates
would now cover about three-quarters of the required O&M needs. However,
the revenue collection rate, which is presently only 60 percent, needs to be
further improved.
! The Andhra Pradesh Farmers Management of Irrigation System Act was
legislated by the State Assembly in June 1997 to introduce participatory
management in the sector.
iO Over 10,000 WUAs were constituted in August 1997 covering the entire
surface irrigation sector. State-wide elections were held for the membe-s of
WUAs. A trining program for the managers of WUAs was started in October
1997. The WUAs will progressively take over the responsibility for the
mannaement and maintenance of the irrigation distribution network in the
state.
- A Water Charges Review Committee (WCRC) was constituted in December
1997. It will, on an annual basis, review and make recommendations on all
aspects of water charges and maintenance funding on an annual basis.
;  A policy statement for the irrigation sector, "Reforming the Irrigation Sector
for Sustainable Management and Development" was approved in May 1998 to
initiate discussion on the reform strategy and provide a fiamework for the
irrigation sector reforms.
Other sector policies
5.    We have launched a variety of new initiatives to take advantage of the emerging
opportunities following from economnic liberalization. Important among these are the
following:
*' We have streamlined the policies and procedures to attract private investment,
both domestic and foreign, into the state. I am personally chairing a high
powered State Investment Promotion Board, which acts as a one-stop shop for
according all approvals and clearances required by potential investors.
contd...



~ 5 -                         Annex 13
page 5 of 11
Recognizing the role of information technology as a new growth engine, we
have endeavored to create a policy and operational environment that would
attract entrepreneurs from across the world. The Software Development Park,
which will be commissioned in Hyderabad by October 1998, is attracting
interest from leading international software companies. Microsoft has already
decided to open a Software Development Centre in the park, the first of its
kind outside the USA.
* We are actively encouraging private sector participation in infrastructure
development. The first two private power projects in the country that have
gone on stream are located in AP. We have entrusted development of a new
port and the management of an existing port to private initiative. In the roads
sector, management of some existing roads and construction of new stretches
have been given to the private sector.
Impact of the r eforms
6.    The impact of these reforms has been positive. The fiscal deficit has been brought
down from 3.8 percent of GSDP in 1994-95 to 3.0 percent in 1997-98. The revenue
deficit and the primary deficit have also been reduced from 1.2 percent and 1.8 percent of
GSDP to 0.3 percenit and 0.7 percent, respectively, in the same period. The business
community reacted positively to the policy initiatives. AP has become one of the leading
states in attracting new investment. Growth has accelerated. The state's GSDP has
recorded an average 6.0 percent growth in the past 3 years compared to 4.1 percent in the
first half of 1990s.
Reform agenda aheasd
7.    The above measures have made a significant positive impact on revenue
mobilization, expenditure restructuring, and efficient provision of infrastructure services.
Even so, our Govemrnent recognizes that this is only a beginning and that much more
needs to be done. Accordingly, we intend to widen and deepen the process of fiscal
adjustment and sector reforms to restore the state finances to robust health, to put the
state on a high and sustainable growth path, to accelerate poverty alleviation, and to close
the gap between AP and the rest of the country in economic and social development. The
reform program, which will be implemented over the next 5 years, has the following six
main components:
a) Fiscal deficit reduction,
b) Expenditure restructuring;
c) Expenditure management;
contd...



- 6 -                            Annex 13
page 6 of 11
d) Revenue augmentation;
e) Public enterprise reform; and
f) Growth enhancing sector policies.
Fiscal deficit reduction
8.    A key component of our fiscal reforms is to keep the state's debt and interest
payments at a sustainable level. To achieve this objective, we plan to reduce the fiscal
deficit by 0.5 percentage points in the program period from an estimated 3.0 percent of the
state's GSDP in 1997-98 according to the following annual targets: 3.0 percent in 1998-
99, 3.4 percent in 1999-00, 2.9 percent in 2000-01, 2.7 percent in 2001-02, and 2.5
percent in 2002-03. This, we expect, would keep the debt/GSDP ratio at about 24
percent, which is below the average of the major states in India. We will also restrict
exteniding Government guarantees for debt raised by public enterprises to maintain the
guarantees to GSDP ratio around the present average of 9 percent. In addition, we plan
to achieve a positive revenue balance of 0.4 percent of GSDP in 2000-01 and keep it at
least at that level thereafter.
9.    As the above annual targets show, reduction in the fiscal deficit will not follow a
smooth trend because of the expected salary increase for the state government employees,
which has become inevitable following the large pay revision by the Central Government.
The fiscal deficit may actually deteriorate in 1999-00, the year the pay award is expected
to be implemented. However, the Government will make every effort to ensure that the
salary bill stays at a sustainable level in the budget and the expected increase does not
adversely affect priority expenditure. The Government will consider all necessary
measures to mitigate the impact including spreading the payment over a period of time and
introduction of VRS in some departments in the course of time. After the second year of
the reform program, we expect the fiscal deficit to decline to 2.5 percent as indicated
above.
10.   The planned reduction in the fiscal deficit will come 'mainly from an increase in
revenue rather than a reduction in expenditure. We expect the revenue/GSDP ratio to
increase by 1.7 percentage points over the next 5 years, which would enable the state to
increase total expenditure by 1.2 points (mainly to improve the social and physical
infrastructure) while reducing the fiscal deficit by 0.5 points over the program period.
11.   The above fiscal correction targets do not reflect the budgetary impact of the
planned financial restructuring of APSEB. As a part of the power sector restructuring
program, we are preparing a financial restructuring plan for APSEB, which, we expect,
will have significant implications for the budget in the initial years of implementation of the
power sector reform program. This impact and its financing will be separately considered
when the details of the APSEB's financial restructuring plan is prepared and discussed
with the Bank in the context of the proposed power sector loan.
contd...



7 -                              Annex 13
page 7 of 11
Expenditure restructuring
12.   At about 17-18 percent of GSDP, public expenditure in AP is not excessive. What
is, in fact, required is not a reduction in public expenditure, but a radical change in its
composition aimed at reducing the share of interest payments, untargeted subsidies, etc.,
in total expenditure with corresponding increase in expenditure on operation and
maintenance, social sectors and infrastructure. This restructuring would significantly
improve the development impact of public expenditure and ensure that adequate budgetary
funds are available to complete and maintain priority projects. The following are the main
elements of our expenditure restructuring package.
13.   Rice subsidy: As noted earlier, the Government has already reduced the budgetary
impact of the rice scheme. The program now covers about 70 percent of the population.
Further rationalization of the scheme in both design and implementation to better target
the subsidy to the poor is under contemplation. In particular, the Government intends to:
(a) eliminate the bogus cards and keep the rice subsidy at current level as far as possible;
and (b) strengthen the existing food committees at all levels to increase representation of
women's groups to better monitor the program from the perspective of beneficiaries. In
addition, a study will be undertaken to assess the impact of controls on rice sales on the
AP economy in general and on farmers in particular.
14.   Government staffsize: Employment in the Government grew by about 3.7 percent
a year in the 1980s and early part of 1990s. As a result, the salary bill has been consuming
about half of the state's revenue. The measures taken in recent years have already made a
significant impact in containing this unsustainable growth. Reforms will continue to reduce
the size of government staff and to change its composition. Taking advantage of the
natural attrition rate of about 2.0 percent a year, employment in the government will be
reduced by 2.5 percent over the next 5 years, after allowing for a significant increase in
employment in the primary education and health sectors. This will be achieved by a 1.9
percent annual reduction of employment in all sectors excluding primary education. The
planned staff reduction is expected to reduce the salary bill/GSDP ratio from the present
5.3 percent to 5.0 percent by the end of the project period, although some increase is
expected in the next two years as a result of the salary increase referred to above. We are
also planning to initiate a study for reforming the pension system-L
15.   Allocationsfior operation and maintenance (O&M) works: Budgetary allocations
for non- salary O&M declined from 1.4 percent of GSDP in 1990-91 to 1.2 percent in
1997-98. This has substantially reduced the efficiency of public assets in physical and
social infrastructure. Inadequate O&M spending is a conmmon problem in all subsectors
but particularly acute ir. irrigation and roads. Actual O&M allocations are far short of
established norms. Moreover, a large proportion of these funds is spent on salaries. The
Government plans to bifurcate the O&M budget into works and salaries and to raise the
contd...



-8-                             Annex 13
page 8 of 11
works component to the required norms to enable efficient utilization of public
investrnent, particularly in irrigation and roads. The Government intends to increase total
non-salary O&M expenditure from 1.2 percent of GSDP in 1997-98 to 2.2 percent in the
next 3-4 years and to keep it at least at that level thereafter.
16.   Allocation for education and health:  Social development indicators in AP,
particularly in education, are presently below the national average.  Allocations,
particularly for teaching and health material, are below the required norms and declining.
Total expenditure on education and health, for example, declined from 4.1 percent of
GSDP in 1990-91 to 3.6 percent in 1997-98. The reform program includes a substantial
increase in allocations for education and health with particular emphasis on achieving
universal primary education, girls' education, and strengthening primary health care
services. The Government is planning to increase public expenditure on primary education
and primary health from 0.9 percent of GSDP in 1997-98 to 1.8 percent by the end of the
program period. This will be supported by policy reforms in both sectors to increase the
quality, reach and effectiveness of the service.
17.   Capital investment: Expenditure on capital outlays (mainly direct government
investment in infrastructure) declined from 1.6 percent of GSDP in 1990-91 to 1.1 percent
in 1997-98. This has created a large infrastructure gap in the state and has become a
serious obstacle for economic and social development. The required investment in power,
roads, irrigation, and ports would be about Rs. 11,000 crores a year over the next 5-6
years. The present capital budget of the state is about 15 percent of this amount. The
Government is planning to increase the capital outlays from 1.1 percent of GSDP in 1997-
98 to 2.2 percent by 2000-01 and to further increase it to 2.5 percent by 2002-03. It is
clear, however, that public funds alone are not sufficient to meet the needs. Accordingly,
policies governing the infrastructure sectors arei being reformed to encourage private
investment, particularly in the power, road and port sectors.
Expenditure management
18.   The following will be the main elements of the program for improvement in
expenditure management:
*  Emphasis on better maintenance of the existing assets in preference to starting
new projects;
*  Completion of ongoing projects before making fresh commitments;
*  Selection of new projects and schemes on strict cost-benefit criteria, while
taking into account both positive and negative externalities;
*  Zero-based budgeting to evaluate every scheme and phase out ineffective ones;
and
* Budgeting based on a realistic estimate of resources so as not to overstretch
commitments.
contd...



- 9 -                          Annex 13
page 9 of 11
19.   The Government will seek technical assistance to improve the budgetary process
and expenditure management to achieve these objectives.
Revenue augnentation
20.   The pressing problem on the revenue side is the declining revenue to GSDP ratio.
The state's own revenue to GSDP ratio came down from 9.1 percent in 1990-91 to 8.8
percent in 1997-98. Transfers from the Center also declined from 5.6 percent of GSDP
to 5.2 percent, in the same period. The Govermment is determined to raise the state's own
revenue to GSDP ratio to a sustainable level through reformring the tax system and
strengthening the cost recovery efforts, particularly in the infrastructure sectors. Transfers
from the Center are also expected to increase because of the expected implementation of
the new devolution formula recommended by the 1 0th Finance Commission.
21.   The tax reform strategy will concentrate more on systemic changes (simplification,
base broadening, and rnore effective administration) rather than on rate increases. A key
tax reform under consideration is the introduction of a VAT to replace the general sales
tax, which accounts for about two-thirds of the state's total tax revenue. This would
require wide public discussion and adequate preparation for about 2 years under a
technical assistance which will include administrative reforms and training of staff and tax-
payers.
Public enterprise reform
22.   To reduce the budgetary cost of public enterprises, a privatization and reform
program is urgently needed. The Government wiMl continue irnplementing the program it
has introduced earlier. To ensure success, the administrative and institutional
arrangements lo design and imnplement the public enterprise reform will be substantially
improved. The Goverranent has set up a Cabinet sub-committee to be responsible for
irnplementing the progran. An Implementation Unit has been established in the Public
Enterprise Managemernt Bureau (PEMB) to support the Cabinet sub-committee. The
Implementation Unit and the PEMB will be strengthened under technical assistance to
perform the new broader role effectively.
23.   The Governmenrt is adopting a gradual and phased approach to the public
enterprise reform so as to build not only the institutional capacity for reform
implementation but also to generate public support for the reform process by
demonstrating the benefits of reform as well as the government's endeavor to contain and
mitigate social trauma that sometimes accompanies reform. As an initial step, 12 medium
and small size companies will be restructured and privatized in the next 3-4 years. A
safety-net program has been prepared to minimize the possible social imnpact of this
program, which includes counseling, financial advice, and retraining support. In the second
contd...



-10-                             Annex 13
page 10 of 11
phase, ari action plan will be prepared for the rest of the enterprises and cooperatives in
the sugar and spinning sectors.
Growth enhancing sector policies
24. Power sector: The medium-term reform program of the Government includes
establishnent of an independent and transparent regulatory body, unbundling of
generation, transmission  and distibution, privatization of distrbution, if necessary,
corporationalization of companies that remaain in the public sector and managing them as
commerc:ial entities, and financial restructuring of APSEB. The Government is separately
discussing the strategy for the power sector reforns with the Bank.
25.   Irrigation: The Government will continue improving the policy and institutional
environment in the irrigation sector. In particular, (a) the efficiency of collection will be
increased to at least 90 percent by March 31, 2001; (b) WCRC will be fully
operationalized to make annual recommendations regarding the water rates to be levied
and expenditure requirements for O&M; (c) cost sharing of 15 percent will be required for
rehabilitation and system improvement works at the WUA level; (d) responsibility of
collection of water charges will be progressively transferred to WUAs; (e) on a pilot basis,
collection of water charges on volumetric basis by WUAs will be introduced; and (f)
transfer of O&M responsibility to WUAs will be completed.
World Bank support
26.    The Government is committed to the above program, and will make every effort
to raise the necessary resources to implement it effectively. The World Bank support
through the Andhra Pradesh Economic Restructuring Loan is requested to supplement the
Government's own resources. The Bank funds will be utilized for the following purposes:
(a) Primary education: significant progress towards universal primary education with
particular focus on the girl child through expansion of the DPEP program; (b) Primary
health: Improving the quality, reach and effectiveness of the primary public health
services; (c) Nutrition: improving the nutrition and health status of young children and
women by expanding the Integrated Child Development Scheme, and improving service
delivery; (d) Roads: Increasing expenditure on non-wage O&M works in the roads
sector, upgrading selected rural roads and improving the management of road
maintemnnce; (e) Irrigation: Raising O&M expenditures in the irrigation sector, to the
required levels and rehabilitating selected schemes; and (a) Public enterprise reform:
Financing VRS in enterprises that are proposed to be privatized or restructured.
27.   Technical assistance will also be needed to support implementation of various
components of the programn. The following three areas have already been identified for
technical assistance: (a) introduction of VAT: to assist the Government to formulate a
VAT preparation plan, (b) public enterprise reformn and privatization: to support the
contd..



11-                            Annex 13
page 11 of 11
Government's on-going public enterprise reform and privatization program by creating a
transparent and effective institutional framework and financing the preparatory work and
implementation of the reform program; and (c) a safety-net program to finance retraining
of the employees affected by the public enterprise reforms.  The Department for
International Development (DFED) of the British government has agreed to fund these
technical assistance programs. In addition, I request the World Bank help identify
technical assistance for improving the budgetary process and expenditure mnagement.
Expected impact of the reform program
28.   The Govermnent expects the economic impact of fiscal restructuring to be
substantial. The fiscal situation will become sustainable with increased revenues, radically
changed composition of expenditure and a reduced fiscal deficit. We expect the
restructuring program will create a virtuous circle, in which fiscal and accompanying
sectoral reforms will enable the state to rebuild its infrastructure, stimulate private
investment, accelerate growth, create employment for a larger segment of the population,
and raise incomes at all levels. The growth rate of GSDP is expected to exceed the
average growth rate of the nation, gradually reducing the gap between AP and the country
as a whole in economic and social development.
29.   The Government of AP, therefore, requests approval of $543.5 million of support
from IBRD/IDA to complement and support its economic restructuring strategy.
Yours sincerely,
(N. CHANDRABABU NAID
Mr. James D. Wolfensohn
President
World Bank
Washington, D.C.
